# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana Database Migration Framework

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in grafana/grafana that implement the database migration framework: the migration runner, the migration version tracking table, the SQL dialect abstraction (MySQL/Postgres/SQLite), and the migration rollback handling.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

## Summary

I've identified all Go source files implementing the database migration framework in grafana/grafana, organized in **13 files** across 4 main components:

### Key Components Found:

1. **Migration Runner** - `pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/migrator.go`
   - The `Migrator` struct manages the entire migration lifecycle
   - `RunMigrations()` loads and executes pending migrations
   - `InTransaction()` provides transactional safety with automatic rollback

2. **Version Tracking** - `migration_log` table
   - Automatically created and maintained by the Migrator
   - Tracks execution status, SQL, errors, and timestamps for each migration

3. **SQL Dialect Abstraction** - Multi-database support
   - **Dialect Interface** (`dialect.go`) - Abstract contract for all databases
   - **MySQL** (`mysql_dialect.go`) - InnoDB, GET_LOCK/RELEASE_LOCK, AUTO_INCREMENT
   - **PostgreSQL** (`postgres_dialect.go`) - Advisory locks, SERIAL, ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE
   - **SQLite** (`sqlite_dialect.go`) - AUTOINCREMENT, pragma table_info, ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE

4. **Rollback Handling**
   - Transaction wrappers with automatic rollback on failure
   - Database-level locking for atomic distributed migrations
   - Condition-based idempotent migrations (IfColumnNotExistsCondition, IfIndexNotExistsCondition)

The answer file includes detailed symbols and execution chain information documenting how migrations are created, registered, executed, and rolled back.

runner. It manages the entire migration lifecycle through the 'RunMigrations()' method, which:\\n- Loads previously executed migrations from the migration_log table\\n- Executes pending migrations in sequence within transactions\\n- Records each migration execution in the migration_log table\\n- Supports database-level locking via 'InTransaction()' method to prevent concurrent migrations\\n- Implements automatic retry logic for SQLite locked/busy errors\\n- Provides Prometheus metrics for migration performance tracking\\n\\n## Migration Version Tracking Table\\nThe migration_log table is automatically created by the Migrator and maintains a persistent record of all executed migrations. It includes columns for:\\n- id (auto-increment primary key)\\n- migration_id (unique identifier for each migration)\\n- sql (the SQL statement executed)\\n- success (boolean flag)\\n- error (error message if migration failed)\\n- timestamp (when the migration was executed)\\n\\nThis table is created in 'migrator.go' via the 'AddCreateMigration()' method and is queried by 'GetMigrationLog()' to determine which migrations have already been executed.\\n\\n## SQL Dialect Abstraction\\nThe framework provides comprehensive SQL dialect abstraction to support multiple databases:\\n\\n**Dialect Interface** ('pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/dialect.go'): Defines the contract for database-specific implementations with methods for:\\n- SQL generation (CreateTableSQL, AddColumnSQL, DropIndexSQL, etc.)\\n- Type mapping (SQLType) for database-specific column types\\n- Quoting (Quote) identifiers appropriately for each database\\n- Database-specific operations (Lock/Unlock, IndexCheckSQL, ColumnCheckSQL)\\n- Upsert operations with dialect-specific syntax\\n\\n**MySQL Dialect** ('pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/mysql_dialect.go'): Implements MySQLDialect with:\\n- InnoDB engine support with utf8mb4 charset\\n- Named locks using GET_LOCK() and RELEASE_LOCK()\\n- AUTO_INCREMENT primary keys\\n- ON DUPLICATE KEY UPDATE upsert syntax\\n- Error handling for MySQL-specific errors (duplicate key, deadlocks)\\n\\n**PostgreSQL Dialect** ('pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/postgres_dialect.go'): Implements PostgresDialect with:\\n- Advisory locks using pg_try_advisory_lock() and pg_advisory_unlock()\\n- SERIAL auto-increment handling\\n- ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE upsert syntax\\n- Error code handling via pq driver\\n- NULL ordering customization (NULLS FIRST/LAST)\\n\\n**SQLite Dialect** ('pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/sqlite_dialect.go'): Implements SQLite3 with:\\n- AUTOINCREMENT support\\n- Smaller batch sizes (10) due to parameter count limits\\n- ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE upsert syntax\\n- Index checks using sqlite_master table\\n- Column checks using PRAGMA table_info\\n\\n## Rollback Handling\\nThe framework implements rollback handling through:\\n1. **Transaction Wrapper**: The 'InTransaction()' method wraps all migration execution in database transactions (Begin/Commit/Rollback)\\n2. **Automatic Rollback**: If any migration fails during execution, the transaction is automatically rolled back via 'sess.Rollback()' in 'pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/migrator.go'\\n3. **Lock-based Atomicity**: Database-level locks (via dialect-specific Lock/Unlock implementations) ensure atomic migration execution across distributed systems\\n4. **Condition-based Execution**: Migration conditions ('pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/conditions.go') like 'IfColumnNotExistsCondition' and 'IfIndexNotExistsCondition' allow idempotent migrations that can be safely re-run\\n\\n## Migration Types\\nThe framework supports multiple migration types defined in 'pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/migrations.go':\\n- RawSQLMigration: Direct SQL execution with dialect-specific variants\\n- AddColumnMigration: Safe column addition with existence checks\\n- AddTableMigration: Table creation with proper key management\\n- DropTableMigration: Safe table removal\\n- AddIndexMigration: Index creation with existence checks\\n- DropIndexMigration: Index removal\\n- CodeMigration: Custom Go code execution within transaction context\\n- CopyTableDataMigration: Data migration between tables\\n\\nAll migration types inherit from MigrationBase and implement the Migration interface, which defines the contract for ID management, condition checking, and SQL generation via the dialect abstraction layer.\"\n}\n",

Dialect** ('pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/sqlite_dialect.go'): Implements SQLite3 with:\\n- AUTOINCREMENT support\\n- Smaller batch sizes (10) due to parameter count limits\\n- ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE upsert syntax\\n- Index checks using sqlite_master table\\n- Column checks using PRAGMA table_info\\n\\n## Rollback Handling\\nThe framework implements rollback handling through:\\n1. **Transaction Wrapper**: The 'InTransaction()' method wraps all migration execution in database transactions (Begin/Commit/Rollback)\\n2. **Automatic Rollback**: If any migration fails during execution, the transaction is automatically rolled back via 'sess.Rollback()' in 'pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/migrator.go'\\n3. **Lock-based Atomicity**: Database-level locks (via dialect-specific Lock/Unlock implementations) ensure atomic migration execution across distributed systems\\n4. **Condition-based Execution**: Migration conditions ('pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/conditions.go') like 'IfColumnNotExistsCondition' and 'IfIndexNotExistsCondition' allow idempotent migrations that can be safely re-run\\n\\n## Migration Types\\nThe framework supports multiple migration types defined in 'pkg/services/sqlstore/migrator/migrations.go':\\n- RawSQLMigration: Direct SQL execution with dialect-specific variants\\n- AddColumnMigration: Safe column addition with existence checks\\n- AddTableMigration: Table creation with proper key management\\n- DropTableMigration: Safe table removal\\n- AddIndexMigration: Index creation with existence checks\\n- DropIndexMigration: Index removal\\n- CodeMigration: Custom Go code execution within transaction context\\n- CopyTableDataMigration: Data migration between tables\\n\\nAll migration types inherit from MigrationBase and implement the Migration interface, which defines the contract for ID management, condition checking, and SQL generation via the dialect abstraction layer.\"\n}\n",

runner.
